class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>+1</span> (<a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">British Summer Time</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Calling code</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/%2B44" class="mw-redirect" title="+44">+44</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/%2B44_1481" class="mw-redirect" title="+44 1481">1481 83</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/.gg" title=".gg">.gg</a><sup>c</sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1">Official for occasions when distinguishing anthem required.</li><li value="2"><a href="/wiki/Guernsey_pound" title="Guernsey pound">Guernsey pound</a> notes and coins not legal tender outside Guernsey, pegged at 1:1 with GBP.</li><li value="3">Sark currently has no official <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domain</a>; <a href="/wiki/.gg" title=".gg">.gg</a> is the TLD for Guernsey.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Sark</b> (French: <i lang="fr">Sercq</i>; <a href="/wiki/Sercquiais" title="Sercquiais">Sercquiais</a>: <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text">S\xc3\xa8r</i></i> or <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text">Cerq</i></i>) is an island in the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> in the southwestern <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>, off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. It is a royal <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fief</a>, which forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Guernsey" title="Bailiwick of Guernsey">Bailiwick of Guernsey</a>, with its own set of laws based on <a href="/wiki/Norman_law" title="Norman law">Norman law</a> and its own parliament. It has a population of about 500.<sup id="cite_ref-jerseyeveningpost.com_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jerseyeveningpost.com-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Sark (including the nearby island of <a href="/wiki/Brecqhou" title="Brecqhou">Brecqhou</a>) has an area of 2.10 square miles (5.44&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sark is one of the few remaining places in the world where <a href="/wiki/List_of_car-free_places" title="List of car-free places">cars are banned from roads</a> and only tractors and horse-drawn vehicles are allowed.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Sark was designated as a <a href="/wiki/Dark-sky_preserve" title="Dark-sky preserve">Dark Sky Community</a> and the first Dark Sky Island in the world.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Officers"><span class="tocnumber">3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Officers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Clameur_de_Haro"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Clameur de Haro</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Periodicals"><span class="toctext">Sercquiais</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Tourism"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Tourism</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Taxation"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Taxation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Sark_Company_Registry"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Sark Company Registry</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Demography"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Demography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-25"><a class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Law_enforcement"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Law enforcement</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Emergency_services"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Emergency services</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Sark_in_media"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Sark in media</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Norman_literature"><span class="tocnumber">13.1</span> <span class="toctext">Norman literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#English_literature"><span class="tocnumber">13.2</span> <span class="toctext">English literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#French_literature"><span class="tocnumber">13.3</span> <span class="toctext">French literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#In_music"><span class="tocnumber">13.4</span> <span class="toctext">In music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Television"><span class="tocnumber">13.5</span> <span class="toctext">Television</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#In_video_games"><span class="tocnumber">13.6</span> <span class="toctext">In video games</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_geology">Geography and geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography and geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_Coupee.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Sark_Coupee.jpg/290px-Sark_Coupee.jpg" width="290" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Sark_Coupee.jpg/435px-Sark_Coupee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Sark_Coupee.jpg/580px-Sark_Coupee.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_Coupee.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>La Coup\xc3\xa9e</div></div></div>\n<p>Sark consists of two main parts, Greater Sark, located at about <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Sark&amp;params=49_25_N_2_22_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">49\xc2\xb025\xe2\x80\xb2N</span> <span class="longitude">2\xc2\xb022\xe2\x80\xb2W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">49.417\xc2\xb0N 2.367\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">49.417; -2.367</span></span></span></a></span>, and <a href="/wiki/Little_Sark" title="Little Sark">Little Sark</a> to the south. They are connected by a narrow <a href="/wiki/Isthmus" title="Isthmus">isthmus</a> called La Coup\xc3\xa9e which is 300 feet (91&#160;m) long and has a drop of 330 feet (100&#160;m) on each side.<sup id="cite_ref-islandlife.org_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-islandlife.org-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Protective <a href="/wiki/Guard_rail" title="Guard rail">railings</a> were erected in 1900; before then, children would crawl across on their hands and knees to avoid being blown over the edge. There is a narrow concrete road covering the entirety of the isthmus that was built in 1945 by German <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> under the direction of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Engineers" title="Royal Engineers">Royal Engineers</a>. Due to its isolation, the inhabitants of Little Sark had their own distinct form of <a href="/wiki/Sercquiais" title="Sercquiais">Sercquiais</a>, the native <a href="/wiki/Norman_language" title="Norman language">Norman dialect</a> of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Sercquiais_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sercquiais-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_windmill_working.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sark_windmill_working.jpg/220px-Sark_windmill_working.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sark_windmill_working.jpg/330px-Sark_windmill_working.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sark_windmill_working.jpg/440px-Sark_windmill_working.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1529" data-file-height="947" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_windmill_working.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Le Moulin" windmill, <a href="/wiki/Circa" title="Circa">c.</a>&#160;1905</div></div></div>\n<p>The highest point on Sark is 374 feet (114&#160;m) <a href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-islandlife.org_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-islandlife.org-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Windmills_in_the_Channel_Islands" title="Windmills in the Channel Islands">windmill</a>, dated 1571, is found there, the sails of which were removed during World War I. This high point is named <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Moulin" title="Le Moulin">Le Moulin</a></i>, after the windmill. The location is also the highest point in the Bailiwick of Guernsey. Little Sark had a number of mines accessing a source of <a href="/wiki/Galena" title="Galena">galena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> At Port Gorey, the ruins of silver mines<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> may be seen. Off the south end of Little Sark are the Venus Pool and the Adonis Pool, both natural swimming pools whose waters are refreshed at high tide.\n</p><p>The whole island is extensively penetrated at sea level by natural cave formations that provide unique habitats for many marine creatures, notably sea anemones, some of which are only safely accessible at low tide.\n</p><p>Sark is made up mainly of <a href="/wiki/Amphibolite" title="Amphibolite">amphibolite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> <a href="/wiki/Gneiss" title="Gneiss">gneiss</a> rocks, intruded by igneous magma sheets called <a href="/wiki/Quartz_diorite" title="Quartz diorite">quartz diorite</a>. Recent (1990\xe2\x80\x932000)<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> geological studies and rock age dating by geologists from <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Brookes_University" title="Oxford Brookes University">Oxford Brookes University</a> shows that the gneisses probably formed around 620\xe2\x80\x93600 million years ago during the Late Pre-Cambrian Age <a href="/wiki/Cadomian_Orogeny" title="Cadomian Orogeny">Cadomian Orogeny</a>. The quartz diorite sheets were intruded during this Cadomian deformation and metamorphic event.\n</p><p>All the Sark rocks (and those of the nearby Channel Islands of <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alderney" title="Alderney">Alderney</a>) formed during geological activity in the continental crust above an ancient <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">subduction</a> zone. This geological setting would have been analogous to the modern-day subduction zone of the Pacific Ocean plate colliding and subducting beneath the North and South American continental plate.\n</p><p>Sark also exercises jurisdiction over the island of <a href="/wiki/Brecqhou" title="Brecqhou">Brecqhou</a>, only a few hundred feet west of Greater Sark. It is a <a href="/wiki/Private_island" title="Private island">private island</a>, but it has recently been opened to some visitors. Since 1993, Brecqhou has been owned by David Barclay, one of the <a href="/wiki/David_and_Frederick_Barclay" title="David and Frederick Barclay">Barclay brothers</a> who are co-owners of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>. They contest Sark\'s control over the island. However, the candidates endorsed by their various business interests on the Island failed to win any seats in the elections held in 2008<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carriage_-_Sark.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Carriage_-_Sark.jpg/220px-Carriage_-_Sark.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Carriage_-_Sark.jpg/330px-Carriage_-_Sark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Carriage_-_Sark.jpg/440px-Carriage_-_Sark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carriage_-_Sark.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A horse-drawn <a href="/wiki/Carriage" title="Carriage">carriage</a> on Sark</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The etymology of Sark is unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Coates" title="Richard Coates">Richard Coates</a> has suggested that in the absence of a <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Indo-European">Proto-Indo-European</a> etymology it may be worthwhile looking for a <a href="/wiki/Proto-Semitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Semitic">Proto-Semitic</a> source for the name.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> This is because the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> were likely repopulated from the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> following the last <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">Ice Age</a>. He proposes a comparison between the probable root of Sark, <i>*Sarg-</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Proto-Semitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Semitic">Proto-Semitic</a> <i>*\xc5\x9brq </i>"redden; rise (as of the sun); east", noting Sark\'s position as the easternmost island of the <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a> group.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In ancient times, Sark was almost certainly occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Veneti_(Gaul)" title="Veneti (Gaul)">Veneti</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (April 2015)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Sark#Dubious" title="Talk:Sark">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> These people were subdued by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> about 56&#160;BC and the island annexed. After the Roman retreat during the fifth century AD, Sark was probably an outpost of one or other <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton-speaking</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (April 2015)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Sark#Dubious" title="Talk:Sark">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brittany#Middle_Ages" title="History of Brittany">kingdoms</a> until 933, when it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Normandy" title="Duchy of Normandy">Duchy of Normandy</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman conquest of England</a> in 1066, the island was united with the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown of England">Crown of England</a>. In the thirteenth century, the French <a href="/wiki/Pirate" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirate">pirate</a> <a href="/wiki/Eustace_the_Monk" title="Eustace the Monk">Eustace the Monk</a>, having served <a href="/wiki/John_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="John of England">King John</a>, used Sark as a base of operations.\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the island was populated by <a href="/wiki/Monasticism" title="Monasticism">monastic</a> communities. By the 16th century, however,  the island was uninhabited and used by pirates as a refuge and base. In 1565, <a href="/wiki/Helier_de_Carteret" class="mw-redirect" title="Helier de Carteret">Helier de Carteret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seigneur" title="Seigneur">Seigneur</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Ouen,_Jersey" title="Saint Ouen, Jersey">St. Ouen</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>, received <a href="/wiki/Letters_patent" title="Letters patent">letters patent</a> from <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Queen Elizabeth I</a> granting him Sark as a <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fief</a> in perpetuity on condition that he kept the island free of pirates and occupied by at least forty men who were of her <a href="/wiki/Commoner" title="Commoner">English subjects</a> or swore allegiance to the Crown.<sup id="cite_ref-BAILII_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAILII-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> This he duly did, leasing 40 parcels of land (known as "Tenements") at a low rent to forty families, mostly from <a href="/wiki/St._Ouen" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Ouen">St. Ouen</a>, on condition that a house was built and maintained on each parcel and that "the Tenant" provided one man, armed with a <a href="/wiki/Musket" title="Musket">musket</a>, for the defence of the island. The 40 tenements survive to this day, albeit with minor boundary changes. A subsequent attempt by the families to endow a <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a> under a <a href="/wiki/Bailiff_(Channel_Islands)" title="Bailiff (Channel Islands)">bailiff</a>, as in Jersey, was stopped by the Guernsey authorities who resented any attempt to wrest Sark from their bailiwick.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sark_during_the_German_occupation_of_the_Channel_Islands" title="Sark during the German occupation of the Channel Islands">Sark during the German occupation of the Channel Islands</a></div>\n<p>In 1844, desperate for funds to continue the operation of the silver mine on the island, the incumbent Seigneur, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_le_Pelley" title="Ernest le Pelley">Ernest le Pelley</a>, obtained <a href="/wiki/The_Crown#Crown_dependencies" title="The Crown">Crown permission</a> to mortgage Sark\'s <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fief</a> to local <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateer</a> John Allaire. After the company running the mine went bankrupt, le Pelley was unable to keep up the <a href="/wiki/Mortgage" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortgage">mortgage</a> payments and, in 1849, his son <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Carey_le_Pelley" title="Pierre Carey le Pelley">Pierre Carey le Pelley</a>, the new Seigneur, was forced to sell the fief to <a href="/wiki/Marie_Collings" title="Marie Collings">Marie Collings</a> for a total of \xc2\xa31,383<sup id="cite_ref-Marr_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marr-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> (\xc2\xa36,000 less the sum borrowed and an accumulated interest of \xc2\xa3616.13s).<sup id="cite_ref-Ewen_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ewen-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the island, along with the other Channel Islands, was <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_the_Channel_Islands" title="German occupation of the Channel Islands">occupied by German forces</a> between 1940 and 1945. <a href="/wiki/Sark_during_the_German_occupation_of_the_Channel_Islands" title="Sark during the German occupation of the Channel Islands">German military rule on Sark</a> began on 4 July 1940, the day after the Guernsey <i><a href="/wiki/Commandant" title="Commandant">Kommandant</a></i> Major Albrecht Lanz and his interpreter and chief of staff Major Maas visited the island to inform the Dame and Seigneur (<a href="/wiki/Sibyl_Hathaway" title="Sibyl Hathaway">Sibyl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hathaway" title="Robert Hathaway">Robert Hathaway</a>) of the new regime. <a href="/wiki/British_Commandos" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commandos">British Commandos</a> raided the island several times. <a href="/wiki/Operation_Basalt" title="Operation Basalt">Operation Basalt</a>, during the night of 3\xe2\x80\x934 October 1942, captured a prisoner, and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Hardtack_(commando_raid)" title="Operation Hardtack (commando raid)">Hardtack 7</a> was a failed British landing in December 1943. Sark was finally liberated on 10 May 1945, a full day after Guernsey.\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:25.5em;border-spacing:2px;"><tbody><tr><th class="summary" colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Sark Invasion</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2"><table style="width:100%;margin:0;padding:0;border:0"><tbody><tr><th style="padding-right:1em">Date</th><td>August 1990<br />(1 day)</td></tr><tr><th style="padding-right:1em">Location</th><td><span class="location">Sark Island</span></td></tr><tr><th style="padding-right:1em">Result</th><td>\nCapture and arrest of Andr\xc3\xa9 Gardes</td></tr><tr><th style="padding-right:1em">Territorial<br />changes</th><td>\nNone</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Belligerents</th></tr><tr><td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">\n<b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Sark.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sark.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Sark.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sark.svg.png 1.5x, Volunteer Constable Forces</a></b></td><td style="width:50%;padding-left:0.25em">\n<b>Andr\xc3\xa9 Gardes</b></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Strength</th></tr><tr><td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">\n1 constable<br /></td><td style="width:50%;padding-left:0.25em">\n1 man</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Casualties and losses</th></tr><tr><td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">\nNone</td><td style="width:50%;padding-left:0.25em">\n1 captured</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_attempt">Invasion attempt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Invasion attempt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In August 1990, an unemployed French <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physicist" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear physicist">nuclear physicist</a> named Andr\xc3\xa9 Gardes armed with a <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_weapon" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-automatic weapon">semi-automatic weapon</a> attempted an invasion of Sark. The night Gardes arrived, he put up two posters declaring his intention to take over the island the following day at noon. The following day he started a solo foot patrol in front of the manor in battle-dress with weapon in hand. While Gardes was sitting on a bench waiting for noon to arrive, the island\'s volunteer <a href="/wiki/Constable" title="Constable"><i>conn\xc3\xa9table</i></a> approached the Frenchman and complimented him on the quality of his weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-Liberation_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liberation-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Gardes then proceeded to change the gun\'s magazine, at which point he was tackled to the ground, arrested, and given a seven-day sentence which he served in Guernsey.<sup id="cite_ref-Liberation_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liberation-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Caesar_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caesar-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Gardes attempted a comeback the following year, but was intercepted in Guernsey.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transition_to_new_system_of_government">Transition to new system of government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Transition to new system of government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sark_general_election,_2008" title="Sark general election, 2008">Sark general election, 2008</a></div>\n<p>Until 2008, Sark\'s parliament (Chief Pleas) was a single chamber consisting of 54 members, comprising the Seigneur, the Seneschal, 40 owners of the Tenements and 12 elected deputies. A change to the system was advocated largely by the <a href="/wiki/David_and_Frederick_Barclay#Sark_politics" title="David and Frederick Barclay">Barclay brothers</a>, who had purchased an island within Sark\'s territorial waters in 1993<sup id="cite_ref-Liberation_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liberation-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> along with the hotels on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_Harrell_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time_Harrell-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Their premise was that a change was necessary to comply with the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> though it was suggested that their objection was more likely at odds with certain property tax requirements and primogeniture laws affecting their holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_Harrell_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time_Harrell-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The old system was described as <a href="/wiki/Feudal" class="mw-redirect" title="Feudal">feudal</a> and undemocratic because the Tenants were entitled to sit in Chief Pleas as of right.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 January 2008 and 21 February 2008, the Chief Pleas approved a law to reform Chief Pleas as a 30-member chamber, with 28 members elected in island-wide elections, one hereditary member (the Seigneur) and one member (the Seneschal) appointed for life.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reform_law_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reform_law-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Privy Council of the United Kingdom">Privy Council of the United Kingdom</a> approved the Sark law reforms on 9 April 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The first elections under the new law were held in December 2008 and the new chamber first convened in January 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some Sark residents have complained that the new system is not democratic and have described the powers the new law granted to the Seneschal, an unelected member whose term the new law extended to the duration of his natural life, as imperial or dictatorial. The Court of Appeal has indeed ruled his powers to be in breach of the European Convention on Human Rights and his powers are subject to further legal challenges on these grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012 the BBC <i><a href="/wiki/Today_(BBC_Radio_4)" title="Today (BBC Radio 4)">Today</a></i> programme reported on local disquiet about the influence on the island of <a href="/wiki/David_and_Frederick_Barclay" title="David and Frederick Barclay">David and Frederick Barclay</a>, the billionaire brothers who own <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> magazine further illustrated the ongoing and escalating tensions between the Barclays and some of the longer-term residents.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 2017 <i><a href="/wiki/Private_Eye" title="Private Eye">Private Eye</a></i> also reported on the situation, following the Barclays\' decision to close their vineyard and a number of hotels and shops they own on Sark.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dark_Sky_Community_status">Dark Sky Community status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dark Sky Community status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In January 2011, the <a href="/wiki/International_Dark-Sky_Association" title="International Dark-Sky Association">International Dark-Sky Association</a> designated Sark as Europe\'s first Dark Sky Community<sup id="cite_ref-IDA_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDA-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and the first Dark Sky Island in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> This designation recognises that Sark is sufficiently clear of <a href="/wiki/Light_pollution" title="Light pollution">light pollution</a> to allow naked-eye <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>. Although Sark was aided in its achievement by its location, its historic ban on cars and the fact that there is no public lighting, it was also necessary for local residents to make adjustments, such as re-siting lights, to cut the light pollution.\n</p><p>Following an audit in 2010 by the IDA the designation was made in January 2011. The award is significant in that Sark is the first island community to have achieved this; other Dark-Sky Places have, up to now, been mainly uninhabited areas, and IDA chairman Martin Morgan-Taylor commended Sark residents for their effort.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> After the designation in 2011, Sark Astronomy Society worked to secure funds for an astronomical observatory on the island. In October 2015 Sark\'s observatory was officially opened by Dr Marek Kukula, public astronomer from the Royal Observatory Greenwich.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark-aerial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Sark-aerial.jpg/220px-Sark-aerial.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Sark-aerial.jpg/330px-Sark-aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Sark-aerial.jpg/440px-Sark-aerial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2211" data-file-height="1458" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark-aerial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>September 2005 aerial view of Sark. North is to the lower left, <a href="/wiki/Little_Sark" title="Little Sark">Little Sark</a> toward the upper right and <a href="/wiki/Brecqhou" title="Brecqhou">Brecqhou</a> at bottom right.</div></div></div>\n<p>Sark was considered the last <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudal state</a> in Europe. Together with the other <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>, it is the last remnant of the former <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Normandy" title="Duchy of Normandy">Duchy of Normandy</a> still belonging to <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">the Crown</a>. Sark belongs to the Crown in its own right and has an independent relationship with the Crown through the Lieutenant Governor in Guernsey.<sup id="cite_ref-hansard_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hansard-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Formally, the Seigneur holds it as a <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fief</a> from the Crown, <a href="/wiki/Enfeoffment" class="mw-redirect" title="Enfeoffment">reenfeoffing</a> the landowners on the island with their respective parcels. The political consequences of this construction were abolished in recent years, particularly in the reform of the legislative body, Chief Pleas, which took place in 2008.\n</p><p>Although geographically located within the <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Guernsey" title="Bailiwick of Guernsey">Bailiwick of Guernsey</a>, Sark is fiscally entirely separate from it and has been granted its own UN country code (680) to assist in identifying this fact to the world at large. Together with the islands of Alderney and Guernsey, Sark from time to time approves Bailiwick of Guernsey legislation, which, subject to the approval of all three legislatures, applies in the entire Bailiwick.\n</p><p>Legislation cannot be made which applies on Sark without the approval of the Chief Pleas, although recently Chief Pleas has been delegating a number of Ordinance making powers to the States of Guernsey. Such powers are, however, in each case subject to dis-application, or repeal, by the Chief Pleas. By long standing custom, Sark\'s criminal law has been made by the States of Guernsey, and this custom was put on a statutory basis in Section 4 of the Reform (Sark) Law, 2008, by which Sark delegates criminal law making power to the States of Guernsey.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seigneur">Seigneur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Seigneur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Seigneurs_of_Sark" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Seigneurs of Sark">List of Seigneurs of Sark</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Beaumont,_23rd_Seigneur_of_Sark" title="Christopher Beaumont, 23rd Seigneur of Sark">Christopher Beaumont</a> is the current and twenty-third Seigneur of Sark, inheriting the seigneury in 2016.\n</p><p>The Seigneur of Sark was, before the constitutional reforms of 2008, the head of the feudal government of the Isle of Sark (in the case of a woman, the title was <i>Dame</i>). Many of the laws, particularly those related to inheritance and the rule of the Seigneur, had changed little since they were enacted in 1565 under Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I</a>. The Seigneur retained the sole right on the island to keep pigeons and was until 2008 the only person allowed to keep an <a href="/wiki/Neutering" title="Neutering">unspayed</a> dog. In 2008, the latter privilege was abolished (on the proposal of political opponents of the Barclay brothers) because it did not comply with the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Caesar_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caesar-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seneschal">Seneschal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Seneschal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Until 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Seneschal" title="Seneschal">Seneschal</a> of Sark was the head of the Chief Pleas. Since 1675, he has also been the judge of the island (between 1583 and 1675, judicial functions were exercised by five elected Jurats and a Juge). The Seneschal is appointed by the Seigneur; or, nowadays, formally, by an Appointment Committee, consisting of the Seigneur and two other members appointed by the Seigneur.<sup id="cite_ref-Reform_law_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reform_law-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, following the decision of the English Court of Appeal, the Chief Pleas decided to split the dual role of the Seneschal.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Thus, from 2013, the Chief Pleas elects its own President, who presides in almost all cases. Only when the Chief Pleas elects a President, the Seneschal still acts as its chairman.\n</p><p>The complete list of all the Seneschal of Sark from 1675 is as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">\n<ol><li>Pierre Gibault (15/7/1675-1680)</li>\n<li>Thomas de Beauvoir (1680\xe2\x80\x931683)</li>\n<li>Phillipe Dumeresq (1683\xe2\x80\x931702)</li>\n<li>Jean Payne (1702\xe2\x80\x931707)</li>\n<li>Philippe de Carteret (1707\xe2\x80\x931744)</li>\n<li>Henri de Carteret (1744\xe2\x80\x931752)</li>\n<li>Phillipe le Masurier (1752\xe2\x80\x931777)</li>\n<li>Henri le Masurier (1777\xe2\x80\x931785)</li>\n<li>Amice le Couteur (1785\xe2\x80\x931808)</li>\n<li>Jean le Couteur (1808\xe2\x80\x931812)</li>\n<li>Jean Falle (1812\xe2\x80\x931830)</li>\n<li>Elie le Masurier (1830\xe2\x80\x931841)</li>\n<li>Philippe Guille (1841\xe2\x80\x931851)</li>\n<li>Thomas Godfray (1851\xe2\x80\x931876)</li>\n<li>William de Carteret (1876\xe2\x80\x931881)</li>\n<li>Abraham Baker (1881\xe2\x80\x931891)</li>\n<li>Thomas Godfray (1891\xe2\x80\x931920)</li>\n<li>Kenneth Campbell (1920\xe2\x80\x931922)</li>\n<li>Ashby Taylor (1922\xe2\x80\x931925)</li>\n<li>Frederick de Carteret (1925\xe2\x80\x931937)</li>\n<li>William Carr\xc3\xa9 (1937\xe2\x80\x931945)</li>\n<li>William Baker (1945\xe2\x80\x931969)</li>\n<li>Bernard Jones (1969\xe2\x80\x931979)</li>\n<li>Hilary Carr\xc3\xa9 (1979\xe2\x80\x931985)</li>\n<li>Lawrence Philip de Carteret (1985\xe2\x80\x932000)</li>\n<li>Reginald J. Guille (2000\xe2\x80\x932013)</li>\n<li>Jeremy la Trobe-Bateman (from 27 February 2013 \xe2\x80\x93 )</li></ol>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenants">Tenants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tenants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seigneurie_-_Sark.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Seigneurie_-_Sark.JPG/220px-Seigneurie_-_Sark.JPG" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Seigneurie_-_Sark.JPG/330px-Seigneurie_-_Sark.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Seigneurie_-_Sark.JPG/440px-Seigneurie_-_Sark.JPG 2x" data-file-width="727" data-file-height="962" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seigneurie_-_Sark.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Seigneurie (<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Sark&amp;params=49_26.4_N_2_21.7_W_type:isle_scale:10000_region:GB"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">49\xc2\xb026.4\xe2\x80\xb2N</span> <span class="longitude">2\xc2\xb021.7\xe2\x80\xb2W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">49.4400\xc2\xb0N 2.3617\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">49.4400; -2.3617</span></span></span></a></span>)</div></div></div>\n<p>Pursuant to the royal letters patent, the Seigneur was to keep the island inhabited by at least 40 armed men.<sup id="cite_ref-BAILII_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAILII-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Therefore, from his lands, 39 parcels or <a href="/wiki/Tenement_(law)" title="Tenement (law)">tenements</a>, each sufficient for one family, were subdivided and granted to settlers, the <i>Tenants</i>. Later, some of these parcels were dismembered, and parts of the Seigneurial land were sold, creating more parcels.\n</p><p>Originally each head of a parcel-holding family had the right to vote in Chief Pleas, but in 1604 this right was restricted to the 39 original tenements required by the Letters Patent, the so-called <i lang="fr" title="French language text">Quarantaine</i> Tenements (<i>quarantaine</i>: French for a group of forty). The newer parcels mostly did not have the obligation to bear arms. In 1611 the dismemberment of tenements was forbidden, but the order was not immediately followed.\n</p><p>In Sark, the word <i>tenant</i> is used (and often pronounced as in French) in the sense of <i>feudal landholder</i> rather than the common English meaning of <i>lessee</i>. Originally, the word referred to any landowner, but today it is mostly used for a holder of one of the <i lang="fr" title="French language text">Quarantaine</i> Tenements.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chief_Pleas">Chief Pleas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Chief Pleas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_July_2011_50.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sark_July_2011_50.jpg/220px-Sark_July_2011_50.jpg" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sark_July_2011_50.jpg/330px-Sark_July_2011_50.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sark_July_2011_50.jpg/440px-Sark_July_2011_50.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2639" data-file-height="3340" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_July_2011_50.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Meeting place for Chief Pleas and the Court of the Seneschal</div></div></div>\n<p>Chief Pleas (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Chefs Plaids</i>; Sercquiais: <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text">Cheurs Pliaids</i></i>) is the parliament of Sark. It consists of 28 members (<i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text">Conseillers</i></i>), elected for a period of office of 4 years. In addition, the Seigneur and an elected President are counted as members; but they have no right to vote. The periods of office are shifted, with the period of half the Conseillers starting in the middle of the periods of the other half. Thus, every second year, 14 Conseillers are elected for the coming four years. In the elections, the 14 candidates receiving most votes are elected. The <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text"><a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%A9v%C3%B4t" title="Pr\xc3\xa9v\xc3\xb4t">Pr\xc3\xa9v\xc3\xb4t</a></i></i>, the <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text"><a href="/wiki/Greffier" title="Greffier">Greffier</a></i></i>, and the Treasurer also attend but are not members; the Treasurer may address Chief Pleas on matters of taxation and finance.\n</p><p>However, if there are not more willing candidates than the numbers of positions to fill (including any casual vacancies), then all candidates are declared elected, without any actual election necessary. This happened both in the 2014 and the 2016 elections to the Chief Pleas.\n</p><p>Until 2008, the Chief Pleas consisted of the tenants, and 12 deputies of the people as the only representation of the majority, an office introduced in 1922. The Seigneur and the <a href="/wiki/Seneschal" title="Seneschal">Seneschal</a> (who presided) were also members of Chief Pleas.\n</p><p>Since 2000, Chief Pleas was working on its own reform, responding to internal and international pressures. On 8 March 2006 by a vote of 25\xe2\x80\x9315 Chief Pleas voted for a new legislature of the Seigneur, the Seneschal, 14 elected landowners and 14 elected non-landowners.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> But it was made plain by the British <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chancellor" title="Lord Chancellor">Lord Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Jack_Straw" title="Jack Straw">Jack Straw</a> that this option was not on the table. Offered two options for reform involving an elected legislature, one fully elected, one with a number of seats reserved for elected Tenants, 56% of the inhabitants expressed a preference for a totally elected legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-Sark_Website_Opinion_Polls_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sark_Website_Opinion_Polls-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Following the poll, Chief Pleas voted on 4 October 2006 to replace the 12 Deputies and 40 Tenants in Chief Pleas by 28 <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text">Conseillers</i></i> elected by universal adult suffrage.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> This decision was suspended in January 2007 when it was pointed out to Chief Pleas that the 56% versus 44% majority achieved in the opinion poll did not achieve the 60% majority required for the constitutional change. The decision was replaced by the proposal that Chief Pleas should consist of 16 Tenants and 12 <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text">Conseillers</i></i> both elected by universal adult suffrage from 2008 to 2012 and that a binding referendum should then decide whether this composition should be kept or replaced by 28 <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text">Conseillers</i></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> This proposal was rejected by the Privy Council and the 28 <i><i lang="nrf" title="Norman language text">Conseiller</i></i> option was reinstated in February 2008 and accepted by Privy Council in April 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2003, Chief Pleas voted to vary the long-standing <a href="/wiki/Ban_(law)" title="Ban (law)">ban</a> on divorce in the island by extending to the Royal Court of Guernsey power to grant divorces.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bailiwick of Guernsey Laws and United Kingdom Acts of Parliament can (the latter as also in the case of all the other Channel Islands) be extended to Sark with the consent of Chief Pleas. In practice, Sark does not make its own criminal laws; the responsibility for making criminal law is formally delegated to the States of Guernsey by Section 4(3) of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Reform_(Sark)_Law_2008&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reform (Sark) Law 2008 (page does not exist)">Reform (Sark) Law 2008</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Officers">Officers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Officers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The executive officers on the island are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <b>Seneschal</b> (Chief Judge, formerly also President of Chief Pleas) and Deputy</li>\n<li>The <b>Prev\xc3\xb4t</b> (Sheriff of the Court and of Chief Pleas) and Deputy</li>\n<li>The <b>Greffier</b> (Clerk) and Deputy</li>\n<li>The <b>Treasurer</b> (Finances) and Deputy</li>\n<li>The <b>Conn\xc3\xa9table</b> (or <a href="/wiki/Constable" title="Constable">Constable</a>) is the senior of two police officers and police administrator and the <a href="/wiki/Vingtenier" class="mw-redirect" title="Vingtenier">Vingtenier</a> is the junior police officer.</li></ul>\n<p>The Seneschal, Prev\xc3\xb4t, and Greffier are chosen by the Seigneur, while the Treasurer, Constable and Vingtenier are elected by Chief Pleas.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reform_law_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reform_law-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The list of current Officers of the Island of Sark:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Seneschal \xe2\x80\x93 Jeremy la Trobe-Bateman<sup id="cite_ref-sark1_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sark1-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n<ul><li>Deputy Seneschal \xe2\x80\x93 Ewan de Carteret<sup id="cite_ref-sark1_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sark1-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>Prev\xc3\xb4t \xe2\x80\x93 Kevin Adams<sup id="cite_ref-contacts_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-contacts-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n<ul><li>Deputy Prev\xc3\xb4t \xe2\x80\x93</li></ul></li>\n<li>Greffier \xe2\x80\x93 Trevor John Hamon\n<ul><li>Deputy Greffier \xe2\x80\x93 John Hamon (father of Trevor John Hamon)</li></ul></li>\n<li>Treasurer \xe2\x80\x93 Wendy Kiernan</li>\n<li>Constable \xe2\x80\x93 Paul Burgess</li>\n<li>Vingtenier \xe2\x80\x93 Mike Fawson</li>\n<li>President of Chief Pleas \xe2\x80\x93 Arthur Rolfe<sup id="cite_ref-contacts_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-contacts-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clameur_de_Haro">Clameur de Haro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Clameur de Haro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Among the old laws of the Channel Islands is the old <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Norman</a> custom of the <a href="/wiki/Clameur_de_haro" title="Clameur de haro">Clameur de haro</a>. Using this legal device, a person can obtain immediate cessation of any action he considers to be an infringement of his rights. At the scene, he must, in front of witnesses, recite the <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Prayer" title="Lord&#39;s Prayer">Lord\'s Prayer</a> in French and cry out <i>"Haro, Haro, Haro! \xc3\x80 mon aide mon Prince, on me fait tort!"</i> (<i>"Haro, Haro, Haro! To my aid, my Prince! I am being wronged!"</i>). It should then be registered with the Greffe Office within 24 hours. All actions against the person must then cease until the matter is heard by the Court. The last <i>Clameur</i> recorded on Sark was raised in June 1970 to prevent the construction of a garden wall.<sup id="cite_ref-Caesar_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caesar-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Periodicals">Periodicals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Periodicals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since 2009 a resident of Sark has operated a weekly online newspaper called <i>The Sark Newspaper</i> (earlier: <i>The Sark Newsletter</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The publisher is a former longtime employee of the wealthy <a href="/wiki/David_and_Frederick_Barclay" title="David and Frederick Barclay">Barclay brothers</a>, who own the small neighbouring island of <a href="/wiki/Brecqhou" title="Brecqhou">Brecqhou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The publication has compared the local government of Sark "to fascist Germany in the 1930s". In 2014 over 50 residents of Sark filed complaints with the police about accusations made by the paper.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2011 a quarterly magazine called <i>Sark Life</i>, which promotes a positive view of the island and welcomes contributions, is published by the Sark-based publishing company <i>Small Island Publishing</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sercquiais">Sercquiais</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sercquiais">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sercquiais" title="Sercquiais">Sercquiais</a></div>\n<p>Sercquiais (<i>Sarkese</i>, or sometimes called <i>Sark-French</i>) is a dialect of the <a href="/wiki/Norman_language" title="Norman language">Norman language</a> still spoken in 1998 by a few older inhabitants of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Sercquiais_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sercquiais-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Its decline has been linked with the arrival of English-speaking miners in 1835, and increased tourism in more recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sark\'s economy depends primarily on tourism and financial services. Sark has no company registry and relies on <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Financial_Services_Commission" title="Guernsey Financial Services Commission">Guernsey\'s financial services commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EconomicPolicy2013_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconomicPolicy2013-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sark is fiscally autonomous from <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, and consequently has control over how it raises taxes. There are no taxes on income, capital gains or inheritances. There is also no <a href="/wiki/VAT" class="mw-redirect" title="VAT">VAT</a> charged on goods and services, but import duties (Imp\xc3\xb4ts) are charged on some goods brought onto the island at around 70\xe2\x80\x9375% of Guernsey rates. However, the island does levy a Personal Capital Tax, a Property Tax, a Poll Tax ("Landing Tax") on visitors coming to the island, and a Property Transfer Tax (PTT) on residential properties when they are sold.\n</p><p>The island has its own tax assessor (in 2016, this remained Simon de Carteret),<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> who collects the <a href="/wiki/Property_Tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Property Tax">Property Tax</a>, PTT, and the Personal Capital Tax (direct tax).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Currently, the Personal Capital Tax ranges from a minimum of \xc2\xa3300, to a maximum of \xc2\xa36,400 or 0.3% per annum (whichever is the lower). <sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, there were 5 taxpayers who paid the maximum amount of \xc2\xa36,400 (PCT and Property Tax combined), and 6 who paid zero tax. Residents over the age of 69 do not pay the PCT. If a resident chooses not to declare the value of their personal assets, they can elect to pay a flat-rate under the <a href="/wiki/Forfaiting" title="Forfaiting">Forfait</a> method.\n</p><p>In 2006, Property Transfer Tax replaced the feudal <i>Treizi\xc3\xa8me</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> This used to be calculated by dividing the purchase price of any of the 30 tenements or 40 freehold properties on Sark by 13. The proceeds from doing this were then paid directly to the <a href="/wiki/Seigneur" title="Seigneur">Seigneur</a>. When the Treizi\xc3\xa8me was abolished, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Pleas" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Pleas">Chief Pleas</a> introduced an indexed-linked pension of \xc2\xa328,000 per year, payable to the Seigneur.\n</p><p>An individual is considered to be a resident for tax purposes if they have remained on the island for at least 90 days in any tax year.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sark_Company_Registry">Sark Company Registry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sark Company Registry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sark  has no company registry, and  no company law. In January 2017, a private organisation called the "Sark Company Registry" was set up. However the initiative was opposed by  the Guernsey Financial Services Commission. <sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Sark generally follows the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_England" title="Education in England">education system of England</a> though this is not strictly adhered to.\n</p><p>Sark has one school, the Sark School, which takes residents from the ages of 4 to 15. School is divided into 4 classes. Class 1 takes children from the ages of 4 to 7 (reception to year 2), class 2 caters for 7- to 9-year-olds (year 3 to year 4), class 3 has 9- to 14-year-olds (year 5 to year 9) and the older children attend class 4 (years 10 and 11).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Pupils wishing to obtain a <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="General Certificate of Secondary Education">GCSE</a> or A-level qualification often finish their education in Guernsey or in England. Since 2006, however, a limited number of GCSEs have been offered to pupils at Sark School.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr Total is estimated.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span
