report.<sup id="cite_ref-census1_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census1-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_ferry_arrival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sark_ferry_arrival.jpg/220px-Sark_ferry_arrival.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sark_ferry_arrival.jpg/330px-Sark_ferry_arrival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sark_ferry_arrival.jpg/440px-Sark_ferry_arrival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3222" data-file-height="2193" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_ferry_arrival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The high-speed ferry service from Jersey arriving at Sark</div></div></div>\n<p>The Isle of Sark Shipping Company operates small ferries from Sark to <a href="/wiki/St_Peter_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="St Peter Port">St Peter Port</a>, Guernsey. The service takes 55 minutes for the 9 miles (14&#160;km) crossing.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> A high-speed passenger ferry is operated in summer by the French company Manche Iles Express to <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> A 12-passenger boat, the <i>Lady Maris II</i>, operates regular services to <a href="/wiki/Alderney" title="Alderney">Alderney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The island is a <a href="/wiki/Car-free_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Car-free zone">car-free zone</a><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> where the only vehicles allowed are <a href="/wiki/Carriage" title="Carriage">horse-drawn vehicles</a>, bicycles, <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractors</a>, and battery-powered buggies or <a href="/wiki/Motorised_bicycle" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorised bicycle">motorised bicycles</a> for elderly or disabled people. Passengers and goods arriving by ferry from Guernsey are transported from the wharf by tractor-pulled vehicles.\n</p><p>There is no airport on Sark, and flight over Sark below 2400&#160;ft is prohibited by the <i>Air Navigation (Restriction of Flying) (Guernsey) Regulations 1985</i> (Guernsey 1985/21). The closest airports are <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Airport" title="Guernsey Airport">Guernsey Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jersey_Airport" title="Jersey Airport">Jersey Airport</a>. Sark lies directly in line of approach to the runway of Guernsey airport, however, and low-flying<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> aircraft regularly fly over the island.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Church_-_Sark.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Church_-_Sark.jpg/220px-Church_-_Sark.jpg" width="220" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Church_-_Sark.jpg/330px-Church_-_Sark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Church_-_Sark.jpg/440px-Church_-_Sark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1782" data-file-height="2262" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Church_-_Sark.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Peter" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Peter">St. Peter</a>\'s Church (<a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>In common with the other Channel Islands, Sark is attached to the <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Winchester" title="Diocese of Winchester">diocese of Winchester</a>.\n</p><p>Sark has an <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> church (St. Peter\'s, built 1820) and a <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> church. <a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a> first proposed a mission to Sark in 1787. Jean de Quetteville of Jersey subsequently began preaching there, initially in a cottage at Le Clos \xc3\xa0 Geon and then at various houses around Sark. Preachers from Guernsey visited regularly, and in 1796, land was donated by Jean Vaudin, leader of the Methodist community in Sark, for the construction of a chapel, which Jean de Quetteville dedicated in 1797.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In the mid-1800s there was a small <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Brethren" title="Plymouth Brethren">Plymouth Brethren</a> assembly. Its most notable member was the classicist <a href="/wiki/William_Kelly_(Guernsey_and_Blackheath)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Kelly (Guernsey and Blackheath)">William Kelly</a> (1821\xe2\x80\x931906). Kelly was then the tutor to the Seigneur\'s children.\n</p><p>Supported by the evidence of the names of the <i>tenements</i> of La Moinerie and La Moinerie de Haut, it is believed<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> that the Seigneurie was constructed on the site of the <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monastery</a> of Saint <a href="/wiki/Magloire" title="Magloire">Magloire</a>. Magloire had been <a href="/wiki/Samson_of_Dol" title="Samson of Dol">Samson of Dol</a>\'s successor as bishop of <a href="/wiki/Dol-de-Bretagne" title="Dol-de-Bretagne">Dol</a>, but retired and founded a monastery in Sark where he died in the late sixth century. According to the <i>vita</i> of Magloire, the monastery housed 62 <a href="/wiki/Monk" title="Monk">monks</a> and a school for the instruction of the sons of noble families from the <a href="/wiki/Cotentin" class="mw-redirect" title="Cotentin">Cotentin</a>. Magloire\'s <a href="/wiki/Relic" title="Relic">relics</a> were venerated at the monastery until the mid-ninth century when <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> raids rendered Sark unsafe, and the monks departed for Jersey, taking the relics with them.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Despite having its own legislative assembly, Sark voluntarily submits to Guernsey in matters of criminal law. For matters of extreme law enforcement the island calls upon the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Guernsey_Police_Service" title="States of Guernsey Police Service">States of Guernsey Police Service</a>. Sark has a small police station and jail, with two (rarely used) cells available.<sup id="cite_ref-Caesar_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caesar-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The island has several Police Officers permanently stationed on it, The Constable (Senior Officer), The Vingtenier (Deputy Constable), two Assistant Constables (ex Constables), two Custody Officers (Special Constable) and several Special Constables.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Sark also has access to police services in Guernsey through the designation of a member of the Guernsey Neighbourhood Policing Team as a dedicated point of contact for Sark Constables.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (May 2018)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_services">Emergency services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Emergency services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_Ambulance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Sark_Ambulance.jpg/220px-Sark_Ambulance.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Sark_Ambulance.jpg/330px-Sark_Ambulance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Sark_Ambulance.jpg/440px-Sark_Ambulance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="715" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sark_Ambulance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tractor-drawn emergency ambulance on Sark</div></div></div>\n<p>A resident doctor provides healthcare on Sark, and is available to attend accidents and emergencies. The <b>Sark Ambulance Service</b> operates two tractor-drawn ambulances,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and is able to treat casualties and transport them to the harbour for transfer onto the Guernsey marine ambulance launch, <i>Flying Christine III</i>, operated by <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Ambulance_and_Rescue_Service" title="Guernsey Ambulance and Rescue Service">Guernsey Ambulance and Rescue Service</a>. A small ambulance station houses the two ambulances.\n</p><p>Fire and rescue services are provided by an independent and volunteer service established in 1958. Originally named \'Sark Fire Brigade\', it is now known as the <b>Sark Fire and Rescue Service</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The services operates two pump tenders and an all-purpose trailer; all three appliances are drawn by tractors owing to the ban on other motor vehicles on Sark. The original fire station was a large garage. Today the service operates from a large purpose-built fire station on La Chasse Marette.\n</p><p>Lifeboat services are provided by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_Lifeboat_Institution" title="Royal National Lifeboat Institution">Royal National Lifeboat Institution</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_Port_Lifeboat_Station" title="Saint Peter Port Lifeboat Station">Guernsey lifeboat station</a>, supported by the RNLI stations on Jersey and Alderney.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_the_Bailiwick_of_Guernsey" title="Rugby union in the Bailiwick of Guernsey">Rugby union in the Bailiwick of Guernsey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sark_football_team" title="Sark football team">Sark football team</a></div>\n<p>Participation in sport tends towards individual sports rather than team sports, but the population supports a cricket team, a rugby union team and a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Sark competes in the biennial <a href="/wiki/International_Island_Games_Association" title="International Island Games Association">Island Games</a> in which the <a href="/wiki/Sark_football_team" title="Sark football team">Sark football team</a> has participated. The annual Sark to Jersey Rowing Race is contested by teams from both bailiwicks.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carl_Hester" title="Carl Hester">Carl Hester</a>, who was born in Sark, won a gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Equestrian at the 2012 Summer Olympics">Individual and Team Dressage events</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> A Sark <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_and_Paralympics_gold_post_boxes" title="2012 Summer Olympics and Paralympics gold post boxes">post box was painted gold</a> to celebrate the event.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sark_in_media">Sark in media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sark in media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>There are many examples of media taking Sark as an inspiration or setting.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norman_literature">Norman literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Norman literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Although there is no record of literature about Sark in Sercquiais, <a href="/wiki/Guern%C3%A9siais" title="Guern\xc3\xa9siais">Guern\xc3\xa9siais</a> and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A8rriais_literature" title="J\xc3\xa8rriais literature">J\xc3\xa8rriais literature</a> has included writing about Sark; for example by such authors as <a href="/wiki/Edwin_John_Luce" title="Edwin John Luce">Edwin John Luce</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Alfred_Grut" title="Thomas Alfred Grut">Thomas Grut</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_F._Le_Feuvre" title="George F. Le Feuvre">George F. Le Feuvre</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Denys_Corbet" title="Denys Corbet">Denys Corbet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English_literature">English literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: English literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Algernon_Charles_Swinburne" title="Algernon Charles Swinburne">Algernon Swinburne</a> wrote a poem, <i>In Sark</i>, which appears in the collection <i>A Century of Roundels</i>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Arthur Conan Doyle">Arthur Conan Doyle</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Sir_Nigel" title="Sir Nigel">Sir Nigel</a></i> (1906) includes a sub-plot where Black Simon of Norwich, a man at arms travelling with Sir Nigel Loring to war, obtains permission from Sir Robert Knolles to go ashore to Sark under cover of darkness. He takes his friend the archer Samkin Alward with him and beheads the (so-called) King of Sark in payment of a wager.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/William_Arthur_Dunkerley" title="William Arthur Dunkerley">John Oxenham</a> wrote <i>Carette of Sark</i> (1907) and his 1910 novel <i>A Maid of the Silver Sea</i> uses the mines of Little Sark as its setting.</li>\n<li>The novel <i><a href="/wiki/Mr_Pye" title="Mr Pye">Mr Pye</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Mervyn_Peake" title="Mervyn Peake">Mervyn Peake</a>, best known for the <i><a href="/wiki/Gormenghast_(series)" title="Gormenghast (series)">Gormenghast</a></i> series, is set on Sark. The book has been adapted for radio and television. The TV series, filmed on Sark, starred <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jacobi" title="Derek Jacobi">Derek Jacobi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judy_Parfitt" title="Judy Parfitt">Judy Parfitt</a>, and featured a number of islanders. Sark may also have been a crucial inspiration for Peake while writing <i>Gormenghast</i> (he lived on the island at some point in his life).</li>\n<li><i>Dame of Sark</i>, the memoirs of the 21st Seigneur <a href="/wiki/Sibyl_Mary_Hathaway" class="mw-redirect" title="Sibyl Mary Hathaway">Sibyl Mary Hathaway</a>, who was present during the German occupation, were made into a play and television drama of the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Dame Sibyl also wrote <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maid_of_Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maid of Sark (page does not exist)">Maid of Sark</a></i>, an historical romance published in 1939; set in the sixteenth Century, it incorporates events related to the defence of the island against the Bretons.</li>\n<li>The novel <i><a href="/wiki/Appointment_with_Venus" title="Appointment with Venus">Appointment with Venus</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Jerrard_Tickell" title="Jerrard Tickell">Jerrard Tickell</a> is set on the fictional island of Armorel, which is presumed to be based on Sark. The 1951 <a href="/wiki/Appointment_with_Venus_(film)" title="Appointment with Venus (film)">film</a> of the book used Sark as a principal location.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sarah_Caudwell" title="Sarah Caudwell">Sarah Caudwell</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sirens_Sang_of_Murder" title="The Sirens Sang of Murder">The Sirens Sang of Murder</a></i> (1989) is partly set in Sark.</li>\n<li>The 2016 novel <i>Iron Chamber of Memory</i> by <a href="/wiki/John_C._Wright_(author)" title="John C. Wright (author)">John C. Wright</a> is set on Sark.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_literature">French literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: French literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Maurice_Leblanc" title="Maurice Leblanc">Maurice Leblanc</a>\'s novel <i>L\'\xc3\x8ele aux Trente Cercueils</i> (translated in English as <i>The Secret of Sarek</i>) features an island called Sarek, off the coast of Brittany, and bears obvious similarities to Sark. In the story, gentleman-thief <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Lupin" title="Ars\xc3\xa8ne Lupin">Ars\xc3\xa8ne Lupin</a> rescues V\xc3\xa9ronique d\'Hergemont from a local superstition requiring the death of thirty women to appease vengeful spirits.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_music">In music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: In music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Irish musician, composer and singer <a href="/wiki/Enya" title="Enya">Enya</a>\'s 2015 album <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Sky_Island" title="Dark Sky Island">Dark Sky Island</a></i> was inspired by Sark\'s designation as the first \'dark sky island\'. Certain songs on the album, the title track especially, explore the stars, skies and nature.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 1986 television adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Mr_Pye" title="Mr Pye">Mr Pye</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Mervyn_Peake" title="Mervyn Peake">Mervyn Peake</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jacobi" title="Derek Jacobi">Derek Jacobi</a> was filmed on the island. The original novel is also set on Sark.\n</p><p>Sark featured in the 6th episode of the fourth series of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Statesman" title="The New Statesman">The New Statesman</a></i>, <i>The Irresistible Rise of Alan B\'Stard</i> and also in the Jersey-based television detective series <i><a href="/wiki/Bergerac_(TV_series)" title="Bergerac (TV series)">Bergerac</a></i>.\n</p><p>Part of the seventh episode of the second series of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> television drama <i><a href="/wiki/Enemy_at_the_Door" title="Enemy at the Door">Enemy at the Door</a></i> takes place in Sark. <a href="/wiki/Little_Sark#La_Coup.C3.A9e" title="Little Sark">La Coup\xc3\xa9e</a> features in a number of scenes.\n</p><p>Sark, and in particular the Gouliot Caves, features in episode 8 of series 3 of the BBC television series <i><a href="/wiki/Coast_(TV_series)" title="Coast (TV series)">Coast</a></i>.\n</p><p>Sark was featured in Episode 3 of the 2009 <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Islands_of_Britain_(TV_series)" title="Islands of Britain (TV series)">Islands of Britain</a></i>, presented by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Clunes" title="Martin Clunes">Martin Clunes</a>; islanders involved in the programme included Alan Blythe (Constable) and Rossford de Carteret.\n</p><p>Sark was featured on the <a href="/wiki/ITV2" title="ITV2">ITV2</a> programme <i><a href="/wiki/Holiday_Showdown" title="Holiday Showdown">Holiday Showdown</a></i> where one family chose Sark as their holiday destination.\n</p><p>In episode 2 of the 2009 ITV mini-series <i><a href="/wiki/Collision_(TV_series)" title="Collision (TV series)">Collision</a></i>, Guy Pearson (played by <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Farrell" title="Nicholas Farrell">Nicholas Farrell</a>) says, "I\'m moving to the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>: Sark. No cars on Sark, it\'ll be heaven."\n</p><p>In John Shuttleworth\'s <i>Southern Softies</i> (2009), John and his crew cannot find anywhere to stay on the island.\n</p><p>Series 7 and 8 of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/An_Island_Parish" title="An Island Parish">An Island Parish</a></i> follows the Anglican priest and Methodist minister on Sark.\n</p><p>In episode 2 of series 7 of the YouTube series by The Technical Difficulties, <i>Citation Needed,</i> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Scott_(entertainer)" title="Tom Scott (entertainer)">Tom Scott</a> chooses and asks questions surrounding the topic of the <a href="/wiki/Sark_football_team" title="Sark football team">Sark Football Team.</a> <sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_video_games">In video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: In video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Recently,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2018)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Sark was added to the milsim <a href="/wiki/Arma_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Arma 3">Arma 3</a> in an update to a <a href="/wiki/World_War_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="World War Two">World War Two</a> modification, Iron Front. The island is made to scale and is fully explorable.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Seigneurs_of_Sark" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Seigneurs of Sark">List of Seigneurs of Sark</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Archaeology_of_the_Channel_Islands" title="Archaeology of the Channel Islands">Archaeology of the Channel Islands</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-jerseyeveningpost.com-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-jerseyeveningpost.com_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jerseyeveningpost.com_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://jerseyeveningpost.com/news/2015/04/09/too-many-people-or-not-enough-jerseys-population-dilemma/">"Too many people \xe2\x80\x93 or not enough?
